<review>Crepes were tasty, my husband and I both got one and I got the gluten-free (rice flour) crepe, which is $2 extra. Seemed a bit too expensive, especially because it's a modest hole-in-the-wall place. They made the food fresh, there was about a 15 minute or so wait even though we were the only ones there. But then they brought us free spicy pickled veggies, homemade salsa, and a different bubble tea sample for each of us. The crepes were very large, too; it ended up being a lot of food! All in all that was a good experience, not sure if the spicy veggies are standard but other reviewers said they got tea samples, too. While we were there (around the time school gets out) probably at least a dozen teenagers came and at least half of them just hung out, so it got really crowded.
The bubble tea was advertised as $3.00/small & $3.50/large which seems cheap anyway if you did want to splurge for that.< /review><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOY29P44RcbEkzLcAxljIBTkL4j2ubfbuTrSeSC=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPug3xsYvk9ZSuVnhQn29-97Ovznae5HDr4YWVw=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pics>< Resp>

<Rating>5< /Rating>< Review>
Delicious tasting gluten free crepes.
Almost everything about this tiny place is over the top. From the diabetes inducing amount of sugar and cream in the sweet crepes to the fake cheese in the savoury crepes to the free bubble tea samples the owner gives you and the ridiculous dance music that's always playing. Amazing!
The ingredients can be a bit plain sometimes, and it's not the healthiest meal, but still very tasty and filling!</Review>

< review>
Little Heaven Deli is a great place to start your weekend off right.

Don't let the hole in the wall storefront prevent you from checking it out - the friendly staff serve tasty, well-made drinks and breakfast foods for uninflated (relative to the rest of the Mission) costs.

Almost all the crepes - both savory and sweet - are delicious and made fresh in front of you as soon as you order, as are the drinks.</review>

< Text>
I been coming to Johnson's alignment for about three years now. The beautiful young lady that works behind the counter is always so friendly and pleasant. It's always a pleasure speaking to her. I'm embarrassed at the fact I don't remember her name given that I visit their shop so often. I do remember John the assistant manager. He is very knowledgeable about alignment and explains everything very thorough. There is also Steve the manager who seems like he is often times in a bad mood. I try to avoid speaking to him because he seems upset most times I'm there. As far as quality of service the shop is second to none. In my opinion the price is a little higher than the average but I guess you get what you pay for. Also they do alignments the old school way. They do not use electronic alignment. I wonder why but it does not matter anyways. Their service speed varies on whether you are sitting there waiting for your vehicle or not. If you wait it's on an average of an hour to complete both front and back alignment. I will return for more service from them.< /Text>

<Review>The Bright Now! Dental on Curtner Ave has been my dentist option since April. the experience has been efficient. For one, they accept my insurance and do not require to have me pay any out of pocket expenses until they confirm with my insurance what my patient costs will be. They did not force a financing option on me unlike other dental offices I have been too that were supposedly within my network. Their billing manager is very clear about what to expect with the time and costs, so I appreciate that. I will say the claims take weeks to be finalized but fortunately I am still able to get the work I need to get done. The relationships with the actual medical professionals is ordinary, not too friendly or charismatic, they are there to get the job done and move on. < Review>
I made an appointment as a new patient with the intention of having my teeth cleaned. I set aside 3 hours of my work day to allow ample time for my dental visit. I was not told beforehand that the appointment would only be for x-rays and that I'd need to come back for cleaning. They were 15 minutes late to take me for my x-rays and then had me wait afterwards to see if a hygienist was available for cleaning, which they were not.

I was presented with a receipt showing a $10 charge for the x-rays and what-would-be $60 charge for when I get the cleaning. I asked them why doesn't my insurance cover this, as my Aetna DMO plan covers 100% of preventative services. They told me the original cost without insurance is higher and this was the remaining cost. I paid the $10 and left.

Over a month and a half later I called my insurance, mainly wanting information on how it'll work to see a different dentist now that I've been here recently, and they confirmed I should not have been charged anything for x-rays or cleaning and that I also have no co-pay. Aetna also has no history of this appointment in their system. I called the dental office back and they're claiming the $10 charge is for COVID PPE and had no explanation for why I was told cleaning would be another $60. They said I'd need to pay another $10 for COVID PPE if I came back to have my teeth cleaned. Their posted online hours also don't match their availability.

I will be finding another dentist and checking the charges again with my insurance. Avoid.< /Review>

Last October was my first visit here. In my first visit I was told I needed at least 3 procedures done. I was nervous to begin with and the grand total was very high. Sitting in the chair and being told the break down, I was extremely over whelmed!! I wish I would have told them, I need some time to think about this first, instead of proceeding with the work immediately, that day. I spent about 6 hours in the chair and over all it was not a good day for me! Bottom line is this, don't let your nerves make the final decision for you! If the total cost of your visit is way higher than you anticipated, ask for financing options! Get to the dentist regularly to avoid Preventable BS down the road. If you need time to make decisions on your dental work, let them know. This will help you make better decisions and in the comfort of your own home and possibly be able to do some research.<//text>

<username>Grant Wasson< /username><date>1487905214078</date>< Rate>

< review>
I claim to be no expert on anything but I've enjoyed sushi in different coastal establishments as well as some of the highest reviewed places in and around San Diego.  Ebisu is without a doubt my favorite.  Consistently wonderful every time.  Delicious, original creations as well as favorite standards.   The close attention to detail especially temperature are highlights.  You can't go wrong with anything here.  Delicious items for a non-fish eater as well such as grilled fare and wonderful veggie rolls.  Very friendly environment and staff.  Great for a romantic date night or a group looking for a fun time.  Try the stylish weekend-open lounge in the back which boasts a stocked bar with some excellent Japanese whiskies, thoughtful beer variety, many sakes, and other unique selections.  Ebisu is truly some of the best dining in San Diego.< /review>

<Text>Came here based on reviews and wanted to try a different sushi place than our usual.

Waitress was courteous and friendly but she was so soft spoken we could barely hear what she was saying to us.  The place wasn't noisy and I don't have a hearing problem so seriously please speak up next time.

Menu was interesting.  A lot of stuff we haven't seen at other sushi places.  We ordered the Tuna & Eggs, Blood Orange Hamachi Sashimi, "Pink Phloyd", and one more roll but I can't remember for the life of me.  Anyway, though everything sounded amazing it was mediocre by taste.  The "Pink Phloyd" is supposedly shiitake mushrooms, curry spicy tuna, with dried bonito, dashi sauce but all I tasted was chicken bouillon?!  The Tuna & Eggs was the dish I was most excited for but the quail egg was just on the side not on top of the sashimi like I thought it was.  I don't know it didn't seem creative at that point. Everything else was just okay.

Overall, pretty disappointment.  I like creativity but if the fish gets lost in all the crazy things added to it then...what's the point?  Anyway, food was alright but I think we're going to stick to our usual sushi places.<//Text>< Rating>

< name>
Walter Macalma<//name>
<date>1402703925555< /date><Rating>4</Rating>< text>
Boy do I feel like a brand noobian. I've been here 2-3 times over the years and never even knew they had a back room lounge/bar. WTF. How is that not in the highlights or tips and almost 500 reviews. Epic fail fellow yelpers, let me fix this. I've got an enormous bladder so never have to go to the bathroom and thus by reason for not going down the hallway and checking it out. I've also never been here latenight, so that's my fault.

Most of the other reviews will tell you of their great Happy Hour and garlic edamame which are both excellent and worth a try, but you should get bonito flakes on those garlic edamame's for some texture and too many aren't giving you the whole story here. Apps are pretty standard otherwise. Oysters are good, but pricey, even by the half dozen, plated a little too fancy as well. They really love their house salad because it's their base to other salads. The dressings are quite good, sesame-soy/lemon ginger is the highlight. Salmon skin is crispy and if you want more substance I prefer the tako to the tuna because the octopus to me takes on the marinade more than the tuna. I'm more used to the traditional Hawaiian style anyhow.

The garlic sauce for the soft shell crab is excellent and not bad on price, actually all the ponzu flavors as well are great for anything coming out of the kitchen. On the opposite end of the spectrum the supremely flavorful tuna collar dinner is to me almost not worth it. The collar is the rare instance where the most flavorful part of the fish is the cheapest and far too often discarded so the price point on this literally seems fishy, sure the yellowtail is extra thick and meaty, but when your amberjack fried and thinner grilled version are half, I have to question that. It's excellent if you don't mind the price. Thick, bursting with flavor and fat and with classic rice and salad it's a perfect meal. Jalapeno Hamachi sashimi is an interesting concept, but I think could be achieved differently and didn't wow me. Ankimo was well priced and often the base by which many traditional Japanese critics compare sushi restaurants. Liked how it was paired with wakame salad. Delicate and something I always suggest to people along with uni. Tempura Shrimp isn't a bad deal as they are large shrimp.

Omakase isn't quite what you're thinking. You only get it with the sashimi option versus the whole menu and to me they under value the option as a whole. The unagi is broiled, but thick and meaty, I was hoping for the smokey flavor from BBQ. Maki is very traditional and the standard nigiri line up with some extras like red snapper (ask for thinly sliced with a touch of lemon) mirugai, both rare even around SD. The specialty rolls are also not as adventurous as other places going overboard on ingredients and profiles, this is a good thing. The ponzu options make their sashimi menu very enticing.

Staff is very friendly as are the chef's, hours are great, especially Happy Hour. I've found people come here to drink more than eat in what is apparently the main room.

Ok so the back. Lounge holding 50 people with 2 booths and maybe 3 tables and the bar. Love the booth for the DJ and live bands that play. The key here is to try their extensive Japanese Whiskey collection, probably the biggest in SD, certainly more than the newer and supposedly Japanese menu influenced Bang Bang. They have more than just Hibiki here and the prices for drinks are very reasonable.  Service can be slow here because there is usually 1 bartender. Don't be like me and check this place out for all it's worth with great food and drink. It to me lacks in d√©cor and the bathrooms seem insufficient for the capacity and I was hoping for more izakaya options. Not a single don bowl,</text>

I love your shoe line, you have amazing selections and wonderful styles. I love love love my experience the other day which was completely by accident. The tech that you use in store is super impressive, the fact that you send that data via email was really cool, I am appreciative. The staff members are on point and so helpful, friendly and knowledgeable. I also enjoy seeing employees learning on the fly and getting trained in the moment. Did I mention that I also recycled my old shoes!! Outstanding. I had an interesting case a few days ago, I bought two new pairs of shoes. I asked at the check out counter may I combine my accounts from the Chicago location to Dana Point? The answer was no, since it's a state to state policy. I was ok with that but still I wondered what my status was at the Chicago location. Thus, I called the national sales line and after the first ring a person picked up, long story shot it was Joey, the CEO, I was so delighted by this phone call conversation. He asked for my address and is sending me something in the mail since his computer system doesn't give him information that I wanted. Really it was out of the sweetness of his heart! The fact that Joey sent his call center home early for holiday is so cool and makes Fleet Feet my new favorite company. I will never forget this and will continue tell the story for the rest of my life!

Thank you to the Dana Point Fleet Feet Team!

< Review>
I must say I was a bit unsure about this place because I couldn't figure out how could they have a perfect rating. Truth be told, they earned every single star.

I've gone to this place 3 times now and every time it's delicious. My friends and my husband have ordered different things off the menu and it's all been good.  I seem to always get the lamb gyro. < Review>
Was surprised to read "cash only" as I approached the door.

Excellent service (quick and sincere apology when I wasn't noticed waiting to order) with a warm and friendly attitude. All public and visible work areas were very clean.

The amount of meat on my sandwich was generous. The quality (i.e., flavor) of the corned beef and pastrami was just "grocery store" deli average. When you took a bite, there was no separate corned beef or pastrami taste or texture. It was all a slightly bland (missing the smoked note and complex spices) pastrami taste. It's important to note there was NO off or bad favor‚Äîa nice pickled meat sandwich. Perhaps steam heat the corned beef and grill heat the pastrami might do the trick? Not sure.

All in all, better quality than most San Diego delis and a much better service experience.<//Review>

Saturday Morning Farmers Market. Three Babes Bakery Key Lime Pie.
I spent the vast majority of my life in central florida and traveled yearly to key west florida and I will commit floridian blasphemy right here on google maps and go on record saying "San Francisco based women and minority owned Three Babes Bakeshop does, in fact, bake a more delicious key lime pie than any key lime pie that has graced my palate on the caribbean island getaway of Key West, Florida".
Price per slice: $7
Price per pie: $45

< review>
Lovey building with some interesting history that can be read in the entrance. Visited the building twice during our visit in October, the first was on Saturday morning for the farmers market and then again the following day for breakfast. The Farmers Market that is every Sunday and Tuesday morning is well worth a visit, the produce is amazing and there are a lot of stalls to buy food and drinks from.</review>

< Text>
Great historical building with interesting architectural details. Fun place to walk around or sit and watch the bay. Not too big for the less mobile people, but contains a decent variety of food stalls and shops in addition to the actual ferry ports. The farmers markets are a fun place to meet and have coffee as the morning weather on the Embarcadero is generally exquisite most of the year. Besides the fresh produce there are multiple vendors offering prepared foods. One of the unique experiences to see in San Francisco on Saturday mornings 8a-2p (also Tu/Th 10-2) and relatively easy by public transit. One of those places where locals and tourists mix.<//Text>

<user_id>116556357736267274624</user_id><rating>5<//rating><username>Anton Vakulchyk<//username><Review>Attention all foodies: this delectable attraction needs to be at the top of your San Francisco to-do list. The Ferry Building Marketplace is a public food market that features a variety of food stalls that act as small restaurants, snack stops and grocery stores. Here you can find everything from staples, such as seafood, burgers, Mexican food and plenty of coffee, to a Japanese delicatessen, empanada stand, nut shop and a cheese and dairy bar.

Many travelers who stopped by the Ferry Building Marketplace visited multiple times during their San Francisco trip. Visitors were impressed with the amount, variety and overall quality of eats available on-site. Though there are formal restaurants available, some visitors say the best strategy is to pick up a to-go meal and enjoy it along the scenic waterfront. And if you're not one for lines, don't come on the weekends.

You can reach the marketplace via the Embarcadero BART/Muni Station and several public buses lines. Parking is also available near the marketplace. The marketplace is open daily from 10 a.m. to 7 p.m with slightly different hours on the weekends. Restaurants and stores, however, maintain varied hours. The farmers market welcomes shoppers from 10 a.m. to 2 p.m. Tuesdays and Thursdays and from 8 a.m. to 2 p.m. on Saturdays.</Review>< date>
